Free Talk

The Grass in the Courtyard is Not Removed, Zhai Fu Talks

A Mirror for Warlords

Mr. He Yingqin recently stated in a speech that the Chinese National Revolution has only defeated the warlords and completed the first stage of the revolution.

We want to ask Mr. He:

Which warlords have been defeated?

Which warlords have been resurrected?

Which revolutionary soldiers have become warlords?

To give a clear answer to these questions, we must first explain what a warlord is. Let me give a definition:

[Overpowers the master and acts on his own,

Squanders military pay like dirt.

Resists not when robbers enter the house,

Forbids the master from chasing the thieves away.]

This is a mirror to examine warlords. Every soldier only needs to compare his actions with this mirror to know whether he is a warlord. If we want to know the truth about the National Revolution and warlords, we only need to hold this mirror up to the soldiers of the whole country and everything will be clear.

The Truth About Xi Shi

— Yi Zang

My younger brother, Yi Chao, previously worked at the Jiyang County government. He recently came to Shanghai and spoke to me in great detail about Xi Shi. So, I take up my pen to record it and offer it to the readers. Xi Shi's real name was Zheng Dan, her Dharma name was Cai Ping, and her historical name was Yi Guang. Xi Shi was her sobriquet. Her father's surname was Zheng, his name was Luo, and his courtesy name was Chi Min. Her mother's surname was Shi. Her father was a live-in son-in-law of the Shi family of Shijia Village, Mengshan Mountain Yang, outside Jiyang County. The village was west of the stream, hence the name Xi Shi (West Shi). The village is also known as Ningluo Village. Because she grew up in her mother's family, she was named Xi Shi. The stream is also known as Huansha Stream, named after Xi Shi washing silk there. This stream is now called Huanjiang River. Some mistakenly say that Zheng Dan is the name of Dong Shi, but in fact, Dong Shi never existed. It was fabricated by later enthusiasts. It is said that Xi Shi's appearance was not very beautiful, only a round face and red complexion. Without makeup, she was already the same as the powdered and adorned crowd. When she was seventeen, while washing silk in the Ruoye Stream, Fan Li happened to be looking for a beauty for the King of Yue. He saw a maiden by the stream, graceful and delicate, with a charming demeanor. Li followed her home and obtained her parents' permission to present her to the King of Yue. At first, Xi Shi did not want to be the concubine of a king from another country, but she was moved by Fan Li's persuasion and agreed to go. At that time, the King of Yue was eager for revenge. He told her, "Can you avenge me? Since I was defeated by Wu, I have been agonizing and thinking hard, enduring hardship and tasting gall. I have no plan to implement. Today, only you can avenge my humiliation and revitalize the ancestral shrines." After speaking, tears flowed like a spring. Xi Shi knelt down and wept, saying, "If there is any use for this concubine, I will not hesitate to die ten thousand times. I hope to offer this concubine to Wu immediately. If I do not avenge Yue's feud with Wu, I would rather die under ten thousand blades." The next day, the King of Yue sent her to the Wu palace. The King of Wu was delighted and neglected state affairs. When the King of Yue was in his twenty-second year, he defeated Wu in one battle. Xi Shi returned to Yue and went home. She was thirty-six years old. Her father had died early, and only her mother was alive. The family was still poor. After her mother died, she was grief-stricken and wanted to commit suicide in the Huanxi Stream, but she did not succeed. She then went to the Qiantang River and took the opportunity to throw herself into the river and died. She was fifty-two years old at the time. Some people say that she did not return to her hometown, or that she committed suicide in the Huanxi Stream, or that she was drowned in the river by the people of Wu, but all of these are incorrect. During the Han Dynasty, she was posthumously honored as a true patriot. Her descendants have now moved to Xiaoshan, and the old site has been destroyed without a trace. However, the Jiyang Zhi records that when Wang Ji of the Ming Dynasty visited Ningluo Mountain, he inscribed the two large characters "Huan Xi" on the stone wall. It is said to be the handwriting of Wang Youjun, but it is also incomplete and unrecognizable. In the late Qing Dynasty, Chen Weiwen, a native of Jiyang, raised funds to expand the land east of the ruins by more than ten acres and built the Huanxi Pavilion. Next to the pavilion is the Xizi Temple. Behind the temple is the Red Powder Pond. All visitors who pass by here cannot help but sigh with emotion.

World Anecdotes

— Hai Ke

France Needs Sparrows: Many places in France love to eat sparrows, considering them a delicacy, just as sparrows are included in banquets in the Shanghai area of our country. Therefore, sparrows are extremely necessary in France. Almost all of the sparrows in the country cannot preserve their lives. Fortunately, they continue to breed, and often satiate their appetites. However, last year, for some reason, an epidemic spread, killing most of the sparrows. As a result, the French, although eager to eat, suffered from a lack of sparrows. Coincidentally, Hungary had an abundance of sparrows. The unemployed there made a living by catching sparrows. They transported the live sparrows to France, where they were killed and sold. It is said that their method of catching sparrows is to first use a water gun to spray water on them, startling them. Then, they use a hat or handkerchief to catch them, with almost no failures. After catching them, they sell them piecemeal to local game shops, earning half a penny per bird. Because the sales in France are very brisk, this greatly sustains the lives of some of the unemployed in Hungary.

Brief News

— Rong

Madam Shen Peizhen, a veteran member of the Republican Party, came to Shanghai previously because of breast pain. She was in financial difficulty and could not afford medical treatment. Fortunately, Mr. Feng from southern Guangdong took on the medical expenses. She was treated at the Sacred Heart Hospital on Ningguo Road in Yangshupu for several months, which cost a great deal. Lawyer Zheng Yuxiu also provided financial assistance. However, her illness eventually became incurable, and she passed away in the hospital on January 5th. There were no funds for her funeral. Mr. Wang Yiting, a Shanghai gentleman, purchased a coffin and temporarily placed it in the Huzhou Guild Hall in Zhabei. Her nephew, Shen Shixiong, has been weeping and seeking assistance from all sides for several days in order to transport the coffin back to her hometown. Shen was a major figure in the revolution. Such an ending is truly regrettable.

Colds

— Qiushui

In our minds, the most minor and common ailment is the common cold. However, in Europe and America, it is quite the opposite. They attach great importance to colds. At the first sign of a stuffy nose or cough, they must seek medical attention and take medicine, daring not to be negligent. The reason is that a cold is a precursor to lung disease. If it is not treated early, there will be future troubles. However, the medical community has yet to find a specific cure for colds. If treatment is not started at the onset, it will be difficult to eradicate later. The reason why people catch colds and where the cold germs are located have long been difficult questions for European and American medical scientists.

However, according to recent news, cold germs have already been discovered. It is not yet known who made the discovery. What is known is that the size of the germ is extremely small, able to freely pass through the most sophisticated water filters used by doctors, and difficult to see even with a microscope.

However, omnipotent scientists do not abandon their work because of this. They have tried many methods to obtain some of these germs and conduct detailed experiments. After the experiments were completed, they injected them into chimpanzees and human bodies to observe the phenomenon of incubation and reproduction. I know that in a few years, there will be a specific medicine for treating colds, and the sound of violent coughing and spitting in theaters and teahouses will no longer be heard. How shallow is the blessing of science to mankind!

Doctors can describe the harm that colds do to human health. However, this is only its direct damage. The indirect losses to the country and society caused by people losing their health due to colds are even greater. A few years ago, an American sociologist conducted a field investigation and published a table of the losses caused by workers nationwide being absent from work due to colds. The loss of wages within a year was as high as 200 million pounds, which is shocking. Our people should pay attention to this. From now on, do not regard colds as minor illnesses and be reluctant to seek medical treatment.

Records of Sights and Sounds in the Old Capital

— Zhu An

▲Toys

In the old capital, the temple fairs in the eastern and western districts, the Dong'an Market, and the various shops during the New Year are most attractive to visitors, especially children's toys. Stalls are lined up, showing a variety of them. I once saw a painting by Qian Shunju of the Song Dynasty in the Forbidden City, depicting a hawker's cart. Women led children, gathering to watch and compete to buy. This is exactly the same scene. If you want to study folk customs, there is no better place to go. To summarize, there are several things that are not commonly seen elsewhere. One is the "Shaking Empty Bell." The "Yanjing Zaji" says that it is made by cutting bamboo into two short tubes, with a small shaft in the middle, connected but not broken. The two ends are solid, and the middle is hollowed out. A rope is wound around the small shaft, and the two ends are pulled to shake it, producing a sound like a huge bell, which is very pleasant to hear. Skilled artisans can throw it into the air, let it fall repeatedly, and the sound will not stop. Or they can spread their hands apart, pull the rope straight, and the empty bell will float back and forth from left to right, without any force and without falling to the ground. This is called "The Immortal Crossing the Bridge," which is a type of skill for street performers. Many children in the city learn it. Another is "Ox Spittle." It is made of glass in the shape of a gourd, and the tube is held in the mouth to breathe, causing a sound to vibrate from the bottom. However, it is easily broken if you are not careful. Many dilapidated shops sell this item during the New Year. Another is "Kneaded Rice Figurines." An iron wire is used as the frame, and various colors are dyed with glutinous rice flour to create figures from dramas, no more than two or three inches in size. The beards, eyebrows, swords, and halberds are all meticulously created. It is made purely by hand, without the use of other objects. It is truly a superb skill. In the northern dialect, glutinous rice is called "jiangmi," hence the name. Another is the "God of Wealth Whip." Candied hawthorn fruits are strung together to make a long whip, reaching three or four feet in length. It is also sold to children at the beginning of the year. It is beautifully named the "God of Wealth Whip" to please women and children. It is neither delicious nor playable. Another is the "Slingshot." Strong wood is covered with cowhide to make a crossbow, filled with mud pellets, and fired by pulling it. It can kill birds and sparrows, and is probably a legacy of Han Yan's golden pellets. Those who make toys are mostly Manchus. They have some talent and intelligence but no permanent occupation, so they use their skills to extend and transform them to make a living. Many of them are clever and delightful, exceeding expectations. I once saw someone in the market using verbal commands to have two insects fight each other. At first, I thought their training was so precise that the price would be high. Upon closer inspection, I realized that they were fake and were pulled by extremely fine hairs, which were hidden in the sleeves. Toys are becoming more and more novel, and the price is also getting cheaper. Making a living is not bad, but unfortunately, most people cannot last long and have no way to sell them elsewhere.

The Story of War Horses and Double Towers (7)

— Seeking Happiness Master Qi

Chapter One: A Peerless Courtesan Leads a Lonely Life Yearning for Her Beautiful Companion, An Overseas Student Wanders and Forges a Strange Romance

Usually, when she was at home relaxing, she also thought about improving her own knowledge. She hired two or three famous professors from the education field, who came to her house at fixed times every day to teach her reading and writing. Even the English that was necessary for foreign relations was being learned. She had originally graduated from elementary school when she was young, and had some basic literacy. With her intelligence and diligent practice, her progress was remarkable. She could barely handle ordinary letters and browse newspapers in Chinese, and she could also speak English fluently, showing it off everywhere. What was even more enviable was her writing of Huang Tingjian's large characters, which were strong, upright, and beautiful, praised by everyone. She almost became a female calligrapher. However, these talents in speech and writing, apart from gaining a false reputation, still did not benefit her in any way. Because she was already very famous, simply adding some refined and civilized titles would not be useful in practice. Since she could not rely on these superficial skills to achieve any outstanding career, she became an antique that was only beautiful on the outside, stuck in the middle, neither high nor low. Fortunately, there was another thing. In order to attach herself to elegance and approach celebrities, she had the opportunity to interact with outstanding young students from various schools. She took the opportunity to make a plan to slowly search among these innocent and pure students for a young man with a solid foundation in morality, intelligence, and physical fitness. She would implement her long-held plan of choosing a husband and assisting him. First, she would use love to influence him, then use methods to train him, and then use money and strategies to cultivate him. She believed that she could personally create a promising and well-behaved husband, achieving her lifelong expectation. She paid attention to this for some time, and sure enough, heaven answered her prayers. A student who met her qualifications fell into her hands for her to test. This person was named An Yutian, and his ancestral home was in a remote mountainous area with strong local customs. He had a large clan and built a famous Anjia Village. His father was the village chief of Anjia Village. He had a solid and spacious residence and two shops in the village, and owned more than ten hectares of fertile land. He was undoubtedly a wealthy household in the area. An Yutian was the only son in the family and was very much loved by his parents. Therefore, his parents hoped to cultivate him into a knowledgeable and accomplished son who could carry on the family business. Since he was a child, they were willing to send him to study in other places. Because the local customs were closed and he could not receive a good and advanced education, they did not want to delay his studies. From elementary school to high school, he graduated from famous provincial schools in the provincial capital. Last year, due to the issue of higher education, he heard that only Peking University was the most famous, so he came north to study and was admitted to a university, majoring in law and political science. Now, he was a mature young man of twenty-one years old. He was handsome, talented, and promising. He had a prominent demeanor, bright eyes, thick eyebrows, a full jaw, a fresh complexion, and broad shoulders. At first glance, he was known to have a strong and healthy physique. He had always been known for his all-around athletic ability at school sports meets. He was also deeply accomplished in all other courses and never fell behind. He could be considered a top student.

▲Continued Slight Improvement, Three Taels and Zero Fen: Yesterday, the price of gold continued to rise, with occasional fluctuations. The overall high and low was more than eight taels. As for foreign exchange, after a sharp rise, it fell again, and had already fallen below 693 taels. However, various parties bought again, turning weakness into strength. The market was peaceful, with fluctuations of only one or two taels. In the end, it was calculated to be more than 96 taels, and the exchange rate also had no special honor or disgrace.

Market conditions are difficult to activate. Although the various shops near the market are enthusiastic, sales are showing stability and even signs of loosening. Both Futures and Spot Prices for Foreign Rice are Soft

Yesterday, the foreign rice market showed signs of weakness again. As foreign firms continued to express interest in selling, the local market was already saturated. Although spot sales in the local market were active, there was a continuous arrival of large quantities. As the Lunar New Year is approaching, most sellers were eager to unload their goods, causing the market price to fall by 1 or 2 jiao. New futures transactions have stopped, and returned goods are also showing weakness. The United Market opened with 1,200 bags of small-grain spot rice, priced at 9.5 yuan. One thousand bags of Saigon rice were priced at 10.075 yuan.

Flour Market Active for Near and Distant Months

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the prices for each month were initially stable. Due to the price of foreign wheat falling by about 1 or 2 jiao, and the increasingly unfavorable domestic situation, market sentiment was very quiet, with prices similar to those of the previous weekend. However, due to rumors that Fuxin's standards, other than the current month, would require an increased price for withdrawals after the current month, the trading firms became very active, and forward prices rose accordingly. Until the afternoon opening, the current month continued to show strong purchasing momentum from trading firms, while forward prices rose as outside buyers took advantage of the factories' sluggish sales and absorbed supplies. Both months showed signs of activity. However, it is difficult to predict whether further changes will occur in the current month, which is approaching the Lunar New Year. As a result, the current month rose by 1 fen and 7.5 li compared to the previous week, February and March rose by 1.5 fen, April and May rose by 7.5 li, and June rose by 5 li.

June Wheat Plunges Amid Heavy Selling

Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market in the morning, each month initially showed flatness and weakness. The price of foreign wheat fell by 1 or 2 jiao, and the factories were mostly on the sidelines. The market for the current month once fell to 3 yuan, 2 jiao, and 9 fen, while forward prices also fell by 1 or 2 fen. Until the afternoon opening, the market for the current month remained stable, while forward prices improved by 1 or 2 fen compared to the morning as the flour market turned upward and market sentiment improved slightly. However, the June contract suddenly plunged due to a surge in selling. This situation with the new wheat is noteworthy. As a result, the current month was unchanged, February improved by 1 fen, March improved by 2 fen, April and May were unchanged, and June fell by 7 fen.

Local News

Zhang Ji and He Yingqin Went to Ningbo Yesterday to Meet Zhuang and Chiang

▲ Important Meeting at Sun's Residence Yesterday Morning

▲ Yu Youren Scheduled to Go to Hong Kong Tomorrow

▲ Sun Ke Talks About Trying to Meet Wang

Sun Ke, the President of the Executive Yuan, originally planned to take a boat to Ningbo yesterday at 5 p.m. with Wu Tiecheng, Kong Xiangxi, Yang Shuzhuang, and others. Because Mr. Sun received a telegram yesterday morning from Chiang Kai-shek's elder brother, Xi Hou, from Ningbo, stating that Chiang was now recuperating in Yandang Mountain in southern Zhejiang, and the telegram could not be delivered, it was decided after discussions to ask He Yingqin and Zhang Ji to go first. After meeting with Chiang, they would inquire about his intentions and activities, and then Sun and others would decide whether to go or not. Zhang and He arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning and took the Xinning-Shaolun boat to Ningbo at 5 p.m. to transfer to Fenghua to meet Chiang. As for Yu Youren, the President of the Control Yuan, he also arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday morning and is scheduled to go to Hong Kong tomorrow to urge Hu Hanmin to come to Nanjing. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

▲ Yu and Zhang Arrived in Shanghai Together

Yu Youren, the President of the Control Yuan, Zhang Ji, the President of the Legislative Yuan, Li Wenfan, the Minister of the Interior, and Li Zongren, a member of the Central Committee, arrived in Shanghai together by night train from Nanjing at 8 a.m. yesterday. After returning to their residences for a short rest, Yu and others visited Sun Ke at Molier Road one after another.

▲ Important Meeting at Sun's Residence Yesterday Morning

Yesterday morning, after Sun Ke received a telegram from Chiang Kai-shek's brother from Ningbo, Yu Youren and Zhang Ji visited one after another around 10 a.m. Sun immediately sent telegrams inviting Feng Yuxiang, He Yingqin, Wu Tiecheng, Zou Lu, and Huang Hanliang to his residence for discussions. Chen Youren also attended the meeting. The issue of going to Ningbo to welcome Chiang was discussed. As Chiang's whereabouts and residence are currently uncertain, it would be necessary to search for and visit him after going to Ningbo, which would inevitably delay the timeline. The central government cannot be without someone in charge for a day. Therefore, everyone agreed that Sun and others should stay in Shanghai for the time being and first ask Zhang Ji and He Yingqin to go to Ningbo to meet Chiang immediately. After determining his intentions, Sun and others would decide whether to go or not. Sun Ke and others expressed their agreement at the time, and the decision was made. They then discussed financial and diplomatic issues and dispersed around 12 noon. (Photo taken by this newspaper of Zhang Ji and He Yingqin leaving for Ningbo yesterday)

▲ Zhang and He Head to Ningbo

Yesterday afternoon at 2:30 p.m., Zhang Ji and He Yingqin went to Sun's residence in the same car to say goodbye, and then went straight to the Ning-Shao Wharf at the 16th Pier to board the Xinning-Shaolun boat to Ningbo. The boat set sail at 5:10 p.m. yesterday and will arrive in Ningbo at 6 a.m. this morning. Then, they will transfer to a car and drive straight to Fenghua, which will only take one and a half hours. Therefore, it is expected that Zhang and He will arrive in Fenghua around 8 a.m. this morning. However, Chiang's current residence is unknown to everyone. After Zhang and He arrive in Fenghua, they still need to inquire, so it is unknown whether they will be able to meet Chiang within a day or two. However, Zhang Ji and He Yingqin stated before their departure that this trip would take no more than three days, after which they would return to Shanghai and then go to Fenghua with Sun and others to meet Chiang.

▲ Remarks Made on the Boat by a Reporter from the East China News Agency

Yesterday, I met Zhang Ji and He Yingqin on the Xinning-Shaolun boat. According to the two, they still need to find Mr. Chiang on this trip to Ningbo. President Sun and others must take on important central positions, so they will not go to Ningbo for the time being. After they meet Mr. Chiang, they will come to Shanghai and travel together. This is the more appropriate approach, so President Sun, Minister Chen, and others are staying in Shanghai temporarily. As for Mayor Wu, he has just taken office and has a lot of official duties, so he did not travel with them. These are the reasons, and there are no other issues. We believe that after meeting Mr. Chiang, Mr. Chiang will be able to follow public opinion and resume presiding over the central government's major plans. Furthermore, when Mr. Chiang stepped down in the past, he repeatedly stated that he would take responsibility and advance and retreat responsibly. In this time of national crisis, Mr. Chiang cannot be indifferent. Therefore, we believe that it is possible for Mr. Chiang to resume his difficult task. Zhang Ji also made a statement about the North China Political Council, saying that the external rumors were inaccurate. The so-called North China Political Council is a misunderstanding of the North China Political Affairs Council. When Zhang Hanqing was Deputy Commander, he had an organization called the Northeast Political Affairs Council, which included Pingjin, Chahar, Suiyuan, Rehe, Heilongjiang, and the three provinces of Northeast China. Now that Zhang has lost the eastern provinces, the name of the Northeast Political Affairs Council is inappropriate. Therefore, he plans to reorganize the North China Political Affairs Council to reduce the scope. This matter is still in preparation and has not been formally established. I also heard about it when I was in Peiping. The proposal for the Taiyuan branch also arose from this. Currently, this matter is still being submitted to the central government for instructions. If the central government does not approve it, then the council will naturally be terminated. The external rumors of a political branch are all false rumors. As a member of the Central Committee, would I do such a ridiculous thing? He Yingqin also said that in this time of national crisis, the entire nation is united in resisting Japan, and the patriotic enthusiasm of the people is commendable. However, in my opinion, we should first unify domestic affairs and reorganize finances. Without internal unity, we cannot face the outside world. Without economic solutions, there is no way to equip transportation construction and all national defense equipment. Therefore, at this time, although diplomacy is important, domestic affairs are even more pressing than diplomacy.

▲ Sun Ke Stated Yesterday

President of the Executive Yuan, Sun Ke, told reporters yesterday that various issues were discussed briefly at the meeting at his residence today. If Mr. Hu, Mr. Wang, and Mr. Chiang do not come to Nanjing, then the government's various plans cannot be implemented. I have now decided to stay in Shanghai temporarily and plan to find a way to meet Mr. Wang to urge him to overcome his illness and come to Nanjing to preside over the major plans.

▲ Yu Scheduled to Go to Hong Kong Tomorrow

After Yu Youren, the President of the Control Yuan, arrived in Shanghai yesterday in response to the Central Committee's appointment, he purchased three tickets for the Great Lai Company's ship, the President Jefferson, and will leave Shanghai tomorrow (the 13th) morning with Central Committee member Wang Luyi, Secretary Liu Kaizhong, and attendants to urge Hu Zhantang to overcome his illness and come to Nanjing.

▲ Wang's Recent Condition

Yesterday, reporters went to Noel Hospital to inquire about the condition of Mr. Wang Jingwei. According to Dr. Noel, Mr. Wang's illness will take at least six weeks to recover. He exerted himself slightly the day before yesterday, and the illness worsened again. The doctor believed that Wang's condition made it impossible for him to see guests, so he declined all visitors on his behalf. If Mr. Wang can rest peacefully and avoid worrying thoughts, he can regain his original health in six weeks, and there is no danger.

Opposition to Seizure of National Taxes

▲ National Credit Heavily Shaken, Where Shall People's Livelihood Rely?

Various organizations in this city were extremely indignant yesterday upon reading reports that Zhang Xueliang and the provinces of Shanxi, Fujian, and Guangdong were seizing national taxes designated for the principal and interest fund of public debt treasury bills. They sent numerous letters and telegrams expressing their strong opposition. The original texts are recorded below:

▲ Bondholders

▲ Telegram to the National Government: Republic of China Domestic Public Debt Treasury Bill Holders Association telegraphed Chairman Lin and President Sun yesterday, saying: "To Chairman Lin of the Nanjing National Government and President Sun of the Executive Yuan: Now that Ning and Yue are unified and a new government is established, the people's expectations are focused on reforming internal affairs, establishing financial stability, resisting Japan with force, and recovering lost territories. Unexpectedly, Zhang Xueliang not only disobeyed the central government's orders by leading his troops into the customs, resulting in the fall of three provinces into the hands of the violent Japanese, but also does not regret his mistakes. Rumors are spreading that he is seizing national taxes, and the governments of Guangdong, Fujian, and Shandong are doing the same, undermining unity and violating laws. National principles and discipline still exist, how can we sit idly by? Moreover, national taxes have already been designated as the principal and interest fund for bonds. Under the current internal and external troubles, we are already worried about patching up a dilapidated house, and this seizure will only exacerbate the situation, making it even more strained. National credit is difficult to maintain, and where shall the people's livelihood rely? If this is not strictly corrected, imitators will emerge one after another. If Zhang Xueliang and others can disregard national laws and seize national taxes, then those who hold the source of taxes can also use their means of retaining them. What kind of country and what kind of government will this become? We earnestly request a swift halt to protect national credit and maintain the people's livelihood. We urgently submit this telegram and humbly ask for your consideration. Respectfully, the Republic of China Domestic Public Debt Treasury Bill Holders Association."

▲ Telegram to the Ministry of Finance: The association also telegraphed Minister Huang yesterday, saying: "To Minister Huang of the Nanjing Ministry of Finance: Previously, at the beginning of your honorable tenure, we telegraphed requesting the prompt convening of a national financial conference to address the urgent situation and a national economic conference to address the root causes. The reason we propose these two conferences is because we believe that legally, the extension of the payment of principal and interest on bonds, which was withdrawn by the proposer, is no longer an issue. However, in reality, whether the national taxes designated as the principal and interest fund for bonds are sufficient for payment due to various reasons is still a significant issue. We hope that cost reduction will be decided at the financial conference and revenue generation will be determined at the economic conference. However, recent news has spread that Zhang Xueliang intends to seize national taxes, disregarding national credit and the people's livelihood, and the governments of Guangdong, Fujian, and Shandong are doing the same. We fear that there will be more to follow. If national laws are disregarded in this way, what kind of government will this become? And the extreme consequences are that if Zhang Xueliang and others can disregard national laws and indirectly seize national tax sources, then if there are those who directly seize tax sources, the government will have no way to hold them accountable. We specifically telegram to request that you promptly present this to the government, rectify discipline, and stop the illegal seizure of national taxes by Zhang Xueliang and others to protect national credit and maintain the people's livelihood. We are exceedingly hopeful. Respectfully, the Republic of China Domestic Public Debt Treasury Bill Holders Association with seal."

▲ Telegram to Various Bank Associations: "To the Tianjin Bankers Association, Beiping Bankers Association, Guangzhou Bankers Association, Hankou Bankers Association, Hangzhou Bankers Association: Since the Republic of China, the government has issued a large number of public debt treasury bills, especially in the past four or five years. The interests of bondholders are deeply affected. If there are problems with the bond fund, national credit and the people's livelihood will be greatly impacted. Considering this, our association was established on December 21st of last year. Although the proposal to delay the payment of principal and interest has been withdrawn, there are reports of Guangdong, Fujian, Shandong, and Hebei provinces seizing national taxes. If this becomes a reality, the fund for repaying bonds will be short. We specifically telegram to request your association to unite with local bondholders, form an association, and actively advocate together so that national finances can gradually get on track, and national credit and the people's livelihood can both be relied upon. This is our sincere hope, and we look forward to your guidance. Respectfully, the Republic of China Domestic Public Debt Treasury Bill Holders Association with seal."

▲ Telegram to the Beiping Financial Committee: "To the Beiping Bankers Association for transfer to the Beiping Financial Committee: We have heard that the authorities, due to unpaid military and administrative expenses, intend to seize national taxes designated as the principal and interest fund for bonds. This concerns national credit and the people's livelihood and must not be allowed to happen. Otherwise, if finances lose their proper course, bond credit will immediately be shaken. We specifically telegram to request strong opposition and hope for a reply. Bondholders Association, No. 4 Shanghai Hong Kong Road, with seal."

▲ Letter to Banking and Money Trade Associations: The association sent separate letters yesterday to the Shanghai Bankers Association, the Shanghai Money Trade Association, and the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange and Securities Commodities Exchange, saying: "To the addressees: We trust that you have received our previous letter. It has now been reported that Zhang Xueliang and Shandong, Fujian, and Guangdong are all planning to seize national taxes designated as the principal and interest fund for bonds. If this becomes a reality, national credit and the people's livelihood would be unthinkable. Accordingly, we are writing to request that your association (exchange) promptly notify those related to bonds to join our association to strengthen our power and protect our legal rights. We sincerely value your friendship."

▲ Citizens' Federation

The Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation telegraphed Minister Huang yesterday, saying: "To Minister Huang of the Nanjing Ministry of Finance: We were shocked to read in the newspapers that Zhang Xueliang and the provinces of Shandong, Fujian, and Guangdong are planning to seize national taxes. It is found that national taxes are all designated as the principal and interest fund for bonds. If this becomes a reality, the national economy and the people's livelihood will be shaken, and the national principles and discipline will be completely destroyed. This concerns the foundation of the country, and we specifically telegram to request that you find a way to stop it forcefully. Otherwise, the people will be forced to seek other ways to protect their credit. We urgently intrude upon your attention and humbly ask for your consideration. The Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation with seal."

The China Merchants Bureau Stoppage Crisis Completely Resolved Yesterday

▲ Double Salary Paid as Usual, Ships Resume Sailing

▲ Commissioner Guo Telegraphed Resignation to the Capital Yesterday

After the entire crew of the China Merchants Bureau went on strike due to the issue of double salaries, the crisis was completely resolved last night through the mediation of Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, and others. Commissioner Guo Waifeng telegraphed the National Government to resign, and the bureau affairs are temporarily handled by Secretary Bao Gongfan. The details are recorded as follows:

▲ Resolution Terms: At 10 p.m. the night before last, mediators Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, Li Zhengwu, Yang Zhixiong, and others mediated at Du's residence. Due to time constraints, negotiations continued at 5 p.m. yesterday. As a result, the China Merchants Bureau and the crew representatives agreed on four terms: (1) Double salary will be paid as usual (half a month's extra salary for January, and another half a month for March) based on the December payroll; (2) All bureau staff and crew members will be treated equally; (3) Crew members shall not be dismissed without reason; (4) If the bureau staff and workers' union and the five dock workers' union are recognized by the bureau, then the crew members' union should also be recognized.

▲ Crew Notice: The China Merchants Bureau crew members' petition group held a meeting at 38 Edward Road at 6 p.m. last night and decided to respect the mediators' opinions and issue an emergency notice to all crew members, saying: "To the addressees: The matter of our petition for double salary is currently being mediated by mediators Li Zhengwu, Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, Yang Zhixiong, and others and has been successfully resolved. The agreed terms are: (see above). The above terms have been recognized by both mediators. We respect the mediators' opinions and, in addition to expressing our acceptance, specifically notify all captains to contact the bureau and await orders to set sail without delay. This is an urgent notice."

▲ Resumption of Sailing Today: The China Merchants Bureau ships on the Yangtze River and at sea that were suspended due to the crew's demand for double year-end salaries, such as Jianghua, Jiang'an, Jiangtian, Emei, Xinming, Tonghua, Haiyan, Guangji, Taishun, Guangli, Jiangjing, Gongping, Yushun, Tunan, Taishun, and others, will completely resume sailing starting today.

▲ Commissioner Resigns: Commissioner of the China Merchants Bureau, Guo Waifeng, telegraphed the Chairman of the National Government yesterday, requesting approval to resign, saying: "To Chairman Lin of the National Government: This bureau has been suffering from exhaustion for a long time. The commissioner was ordered to reorganize it. Since arriving at the bureau, eight months have passed in an instant. The affairs are complex and difficult to sort out, and the finances are stretched and difficult to plan. During the military period, the ships were requisitioned for military use, and business was suspended, with a greater impact. The accumulated debts of past office holders are also considerable, and demands for payment are constantly coming, making it difficult to cope. Fortunately, the domestic military situation has ended, and the people are fiercely boycotting Japanese shipping, so we are planning to develop further, add ships, and open up routes. Unexpectedly, the crew suddenly requested to be paid a year-end double salary. Considering the situation of the bureau, the commissioner is trying to economize on all expenses, and this matter is not only unprecedented in the bureau but also rare in the industry, so it should be carefully considered and not easily allowed. However, the crew did not understand this and went on strike. The details have been telegraphed on a previous day. Over the past two days, I have tried to persuade them several times, but the commissioner's sincerity has not been trusted and has not been resolved. At this time of national crisis, all are united, and we are still worried about not being able to overcome the difficulties, but this has happened. I am deeply saddened and even more fearful. I am afraid that I will delay the bureau's affairs, so I dare to resign and respectfully request approval to vacate the post and appoint other capable people to take over, to meet the expectations of the public and avoid prolonged disruptions to transportation, benefiting both public and private interests. I am deeply grateful and respectfully submit this telegram, hoping for your approval and filled with apprehension. Respectfully, Commissioner Guo Waifeng, organizing the China Merchants Bureau."

He Zhuguo Willing to Stay at Famous Pass to the End

▲ Reply to Zhejiang National Crisis Association's Telegram

He Zhuguo, Brigade Commander of Shanhaiguan, replied to the Zhejiang National Crisis Relief Association, saying: "To the Zhejiang Provincial National Crisis Relief Association: I received your kind telegram. I am honored by your encouragement and filled with shame and trepidation. With responsibility on my shoulders, how can I allow distractions? Zhuguo is determined to stay at the famous pass to the end. Success or failure, gain or loss, are not my concerns. I only hope that my compatriots will rise up and urge the central government to extend this last shred of national strength and protect this last stronghold. I am holding back and enduring the pain, waiting for your hope. He Zhuguo with seal."

Feng Yuxiang's Conversation

▲ Denies News of Imminent Return North

Feng Yuxiang released the following statement yesterday: (Question) It has recently been heard that the National Defense Council will be established soon amid the current national defense crisis, and the central government has decided to invite you to serve as the chairman. Can you tell us the details? (Answer) I have not heard of it. (Question) Will you be going to Fenghua and Hong Kong recently? (Answer) If Mr. Hu and Mr. Chiang do not come north, then I will definitely go to Hong Kong and Ningbo, but the date has not yet been determined. (Question) What did you discuss at Mr. Sun's residence today (yesterday)? Did you discuss the matter of Mr. Sun and others going to Fenghua to urge Mr. Chiang to go to the capital? (Answer) Today (yesterday), I met with Mr. Sun and only discussed the difficult financial situation, not other matters. (Question) Is it true that you have plans to go north soon? (Answer) Not true. Finally, there is one more point: yesterday's newspaper reported that I sent a telegram to Mr. Lin Zichao, saying that I am recuperating in Shanghai and cannot go to the capital, etc. This is not true, and I did not send this telegram. I am afraid there is a misunderstanding, so I am making this additional statement."

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Director Mai Chaochu Took Office Yesterday

▲ Oath Ceremony to Be Held on Another Day

Mr. Mai Chaochu, the new director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, took office at the bureau yesterday and will hold an official oath ceremony on another day. He completed the handover in the morning and addressed all the staff in the afternoon with sincere encouragement. The details are recorded below:

▲ Handover Situation: At around 10 a.m. yesterday, Mr. Mai Chaochu, accompanied by Secretary Huang Shenzhi, Section Chief Mai Gongyun, and more than ten others, arrived at the bureau by car. He immediately sent Dong to take over the documents from the Registry. Mr. Mai took over the seals, funds, account books, and other items and issued two written orders, saying: [No public property within the bureau shall be moved out without authorization, this order.] [No staff member of this bureau shall leave his post without authorization, this order, Director Mai, etc.] Those who came to offer congratulations from all sides included Secretary-General Yu Hongjun of the Municipal Government, President Xu Fu of the Municipal Bank, and representatives from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, various industry unions, and various trade associations. Mr. Mai greeted them one by one.

▲ Staff Changes: The previous Secretary of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Mi Xingru, Section Chief of the First Section, Sun Jianhou, Section Chief of the Second Section, Wu Huanru, Section Chief of the Third Section, Zhang Tinghao, and Section Chief of the Fourth Section, Feng Liutang, have all submitted their resignations. Yesterday, when Director Mai took over, except for Sun Jianhou, Section Chief of the First Section, who came to the bureau to handle the handover, the rest did not come to the bureau. Mr. Mai has appointed Mai Gongyun as the Section Chief of the First Section and Huang Shenzhi as the Secretary. For Wu Huanru, the Section Chief of the Second Section, Mr. Mai entrusted Huang Jitong, a member of the bureau's Grain Committee, to go to Wu's residence to personally persuade him to stay, and Wu has agreed, so he will continue to serve.

▲ Director's Address: At 3 p.m. yesterday, Director Mai convened all the staff and addressed them in the auditorium, saying: "I was ordered to be the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau this time, and it was done hastily. It is difficult to decide and announce specific new plans for the bureau's future at this time. However, I have always been practical in my work and do not advocate empty talk. The position of this bureau can be said to occupy an important position in this city. Matters such as agricultural, industrial, and commercial organizations, labor disputes, and poverty relief are all handled by this bureau. I believe that various disputes in society are mostly caused by inequality and dissatisfaction in economic life. This bureau has always handled labor disputes, and there are a great many of them. This is an example. I believe that these disputes should be dealt with fairly. As for poverty relief, there are beggars everywhere. This is an example of the prevalence of the poor. This is not only an eyesore but also enough to indicate the economic distress of society and the state of being on the verge of bankruptcy. Therefore, I believe that even if we do not talk about ambitious plans, even the problem of beggars must be solved quickly. All plans will be made after examining the situation of the bureau and the objective conditions of all aspects. However, I believe that the Social Affairs Bureau is a mechanism related to all sectors of society. The progress of the bureau's affairs and the development of social undertakings all depend on everyone's joint efforts. If everyone thinks that this bureau is a bureaucratic organization, then that is wrong. The personnel within the bureau are mostly people who have been working for many years and are rich in knowledge and experience. I will not easily change them," and so on.

▲ Staff's Response: After the Director's speech, Section Member Tian Heqing delivered a welcome speech on behalf of all the staff. "Today is the day that Director Mai takes office, and we are deeply gratified to have a new leader. Tracing back to when this bureau was the Bureau of Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce, former Director Pan was the first person to hold the post. Since the reorganization of the Social Affairs Bureau in August of the 17th year of the Republic, thanks to the hard work of former Director Pan, the construction projects have been able to proceed in an orderly manner to this day. The statistical work especially has a considerable position, and the daily mediation of labor disputes, the organization of agricultural, industrial, commercial, and charitable organizations also have a beginning. Social order is gradually stabilizing, and the estrangement between labor and capital is gradually disappearing. Recently, the implementation of the Factory Law, the promotion of weights and measures, the construction of the National Goods Exhibition Hall, and the overall planning of the people's livelihood issues are still in active progress. We have fulfilled our duty as civil servants and followed former Director Pan to achieve this result, and we are also proud of it. Now, former Director Pan has been working hard for four years and eagerly wants to retire, and his resignation has been approved. The Central Government has specially appointed Director Mai to lead this bureau. Director Mai is a revolutionary pioneer, and his achievements for the Party and the country in the past are well known, and his selflessness and fearless revolutionary spirit are especially admired by us. Recently, we listened to his speech, and he sincerely encouraged us with the word 'sincerity', so he will surely treat us with sincerity, and we will naturally follow Director Mai with sincerity and work hard for the Party, the country, and society. Hereby, I represent all the staff and extend a welcome."

▲ Taking Office Announcement: Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Announcement No. 1 states: "For the matter of the announcement: According to the Shanghai Municipal Government Appointment Order No. 3, hereby appoint Mai Chaochu as the Director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, this order, etc. Therefore, I complied and took office at the bureau on the 11th of this month. In addition to submitting a report and distributing it, I hereby issue this announcement for general knowledge. January 11, the 21st year of the Republic of China, Director Mai Chaochu."

▲ Mai's Brief Biography: Mai Chaochu, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, whose courtesy name is Zhongjie, is from Taishan, Guangdong. He is 35 years old this year. In the 7th year of the Republic of China, he graduated from the Department of Arts of Peking University. He served as a faculty member at Guangdong University, Guangzhou Municipal Normal School, and other schools. In the 14th year of the Republic of China, he served as a member of the Guangzhou Municipal Government. In the 15th year of the Republic of China, during the Northern Expedition, he served as the Director of the Political Department of the 4th Army of the National Revolutionary Army. After the revolution settled in Hubei, he transferred to serve as the Secretary of the Hubei Provincial Government Committee and concurrently as the Secretary-General of the Political Department of the Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army. In the 16th year of the Republic of China, he was transferred to be the Secretary of the National Government. In the 17th year of the Republic of China, he served as the Secretary-General of the Construction Committee of the Guangzhou Political Branch. In the 18th year of the Republic of China, he served as the Provost of Shanghai Jiao Tong University.

▲ Pan's Handover: Pan Gongzhan, the former director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, reported to the Municipal Government yesterday about the handover, saying: "Report regarding the handover matter: After my resignation was approved, the newly appointed Director Mai Chaochu took over on January 11 and handed over the seals, documents, funds, etc. Hereby report the progress and request that it be forwarded to the Executive Yuan for record." Signed, Mayor Wu.

National Postal Workers' Congress Opens Yesterday

▲Representatives from Fifteen Provinces Arrive, with Representatives from Six Provinces Still En Route

▲Preparatory Meeting Scheduled for This Morning, General Assembly to Follow This Afternoon

The National Postal Workers' Congress, initiated and convened by the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, opened as scheduled yesterday at 10:00 AM at No. 9 Runde Lane, Fusheng Road, Zhabei. The ceremony was solemn. A presidium was elected on the spot, and a secretariat and a credentials committee were formed. After the ceremony, the credentials committee convened in the afternoon to review proposals. A preparatory meeting is scheduled for this morning, followed by the general assembly this afternoon. As of yesterday, representatives from fifteen provinces had arrived in Shanghai. The atmosphere was very dignified. The details are reported below:

▲Arriving Representatives Yesterday, the following representatives arrived in Shanghai successively: Kang Yong from Liaoning, Pin Zhengxuan from Hebei, Liang Shaodong from Henan, Quan Yunjie from Hubei, Zheng Yipeng from Jiangxi, Hu Mengquan from Shanxi, Huang Jinhai from Guangdong, Hu Xie from Hunan, Wang Yinglin from Jiangsu and Anhui, Jiang Jiade, Yang Bozhao, Qi Qie, Wang Shiying from Zhejiang, Kang Yong from Jilin (also representing Heilongjiang), Fu Dewei, Huang Jieming, Zhang Xiyang, Shi Yitang, and Huang Gongfu from Shanghai, totaling fifteen postal districts. Representatives from six provinces and regions—Guangxi, Xinjiang, Yunnan, Sichuan, Shaanxi, and Gansu—have all telegraphed that they are en route and will arrive within days.

▲Opening Ceremony At 10:00 AM, all representatives gathered at the meeting place. Led by Fu Dewei, the ceremony proceeded as follows (Order of Ceremony for the First National Postal Workers' Congress): 1. All stand at attention and give the highest salute to the Party, the national flag, and the portrait of the late Premier. 2. Reverently read the Premier's will. 3. Observe three minutes of silence to mourn national difficulties. 4. The chairman delivers the opening address. 5. The preparatory committee of the National Postal Workers' General Union reports on the preparatory process. 6. Representatives from each district report on the work situation in their respective districts and the state of the labor movement in various regions. 7. Speeches. 8. Photograph. 9. End of ceremony.

▲Welcoming Representatives After the ceremony, Chairman Fu Dewei delivered a welcoming speech, saying: "World affairs change, trends surge. To undertake the work of ten thousand people is to establish a foundation for a hundred generations. Thus, we drive ourselves forward to create a bright future for the postal industry and strive for the welfare of workers. However, scope limited to one corner breeds narrow-mindedness, and those who are rigid hold only fragmented views. Application values adaptability, and those who speak trivially cannot escape petty criticism. Moreover, to act only when the time is right is to fear the folly of marking a boat to find a lost sword; one wave, one ripple, and the danger of bankruptcy looms. This is like hiding a sword in the city, where the light of the Dipper is close; or throwing jade into the water, where the colors of the rainbow have yet to fly. Though we have endured much hardship, we have not yet reached the highest level. It is fitting that we be like a bell waiting to be struck, or jade waiting to be polished. Then, offering robes and pushing up sleeves, we should humbly attach ourselves to the swift steed; gathering thoughts and broadening our minds, we shall step forward to mount the dragon. Visit my southern village, and come swiftly a thousand miles like Ji Kang. Act as my host in the east, and await Fan Shi's return for three years. The joy of unity surpasses that of flesh and blood, and the benefits of hardship equal those of siblings. May I dare to say that, standing near the water tower, we participate in the administration of the government, and with boundless aspirations, we contemplate the distant clouds and trees. This is precisely the reason why our association welcomes the representatives of the National Postal Workers' General Union with utmost sincerity. Let us not betray our long-held aspirations, and let us meet in this grand gathering. Regardless of whether you come from the south or the north, let us personally experience your great talents. May we together defend our territory and listen eagerly to your teachings. Being inquisitive leads to abundance, and specialized skills alone are insufficient. Taking goodness as our teacher, a broad scope is uniquely superior. From now on, let us rectify association affairs and encourage each other with economic writing; let us recover postal rights and teach me your profound plans. United in confronting external forces, let us uproot the unrighteous and overthrow the powerful. With many paths converging, let us pledge our loyalty and unveil the darkness. Ultimately, let us harmonize words and deeds and broadly implement teachings, rather than drifting like the wind and rain, enduring the perils of rugged paths. Let us emulate Guan Zhong and Bao Shuya in their cooperation and establish an extraordinary undertaking today. Let us meet like needle and mustard seed and pass on our reputation to future generations. Distinguishing between right and wrong will prevent deviant paths, and respecting authority will guard against frivolous conduct. With so many heroes present, who would cling to petty grievances and forget their comrades? At such a young age, everyone must set aside personal grudges and strive to be prepared for battle. With shared skills, good fortune will present harmony. May we, like ordinary silk and constant fabrics, receive the needle that mends the robes of emperors. If we can advance side by side, we can lend our strength to support the wheels of progress. We shall see the forging of a multitude of talents, and the refined craftsmanship will transform the old. It is rare to have like-minded comrades visit; I respectfully bow my hands and offer my congratulations for the new year." Then, representatives delivered responses and reported on the association affairs and labor movement situation in various regions. The ceremony then ended.

▲Review of Proposals The presidium was then formed, with Fu Dewei and two others (names temporarily omitted) as members. A secretariat and a credentials committee were also established. The secretariat consisted of six members, and the credentials committee was divided into four groups, each with six members (names temporarily omitted). The credentials committee immediately began reviewing proposals in the afternoon, preparing them for the preparatory meeting to be held this morning. After detailed sorting, the proposals will be submitted to the general assembly for discussion. The conference is still scheduled for five days, with the official general assembly starting this afternoon and continuing until the 15th. However, due to the large number of proposals from various districts, which may require lengthy discussions, the conference will be extended by one day to the 16th.

▲Collection of Congratulatory Telegrams 1. The Preparatory Committee of the All-China Postal Workers' General Union and the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union sent a telegram to the National Postal Workers' Congress yesterday, stating: "To the National Postal Workers' Congress: Congratulations on the opening of the congress, the creation of a new framework, the strict organization, and the collective wisdom of all. Our unions share the same origin and have long endured hardships together. We sincerely hope to eliminate regional barriers, forge close ties of solidarity, and lay a solid foundation for our postal service with one heart and one mind. We send this telegram to express our congratulations and wish you a boundless future. Sincerely, The Preparatory Committee of the All-China Postal Workers' General Union." 2. "To the National Postal Workers' Congress: The development of our postal service relies on organization. The great achievements of the General Union were created two years ago. Today's congress further consolidates this foundation. With one heart and one mind, we forge ahead together. We send this telegram to express our congratulations and wish you continuous progress. Sincerely, The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union."

Public Concession Studies Ways to Make Up for Budget Shortfall

▲Increase in Police Rates Considered

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession is considering increasing the police rates by 2% from 14% to 16% in order to offset a budget shortfall for next year, despite making painful cuts in expenditures. This increase is estimated to generate an additional revenue of 1.2 million taels. After the council's Finance Committee carefully studied the issue based on a report from the accounting department, the proposal was thoroughly discussed at the last board meeting. Due to the significant implications, a decision was not immediately made and will be further considered after receiving detailed opinions from the Chinese councilors.

According to a statement released yesterday by the council's Information Office, the council's board is carefully studying the financial situation. In September of last year, the accounting department predicted a deficit of 600,000 taels at the end of the current fiscal year. However, by cutting expenditures in various departments and with improvements in exchange rates, the accounting director reported at a recent meeting of the Finance Committee that the projected deficit for this year has been reduced to less than 200,000 taels. However, the 1932 budget must not only cover this deficit but also raise an additional 2.3 million taels compared to this year. This is because in 1930, 2.3 million taels were carried over from previous years, which will not be available for the 1932 budget. Additionally, in 1931, 500,000 taels from accumulated rice reserves could be allocated, while it is estimated that regular income for 1932 will increase by 400,000 taels. The budget for each department for 1932 has just been completed, and it is difficult to predict the extent to which further cuts can be made. As it stands, the Public Works Department's budget is similar to that of 1931, but 200,000 taels with investment characteristics have been moved to the special expenditure category. The budget for the Health Department is approximately 150,000 taels higher than in 1931. Regarding education, there is a proposal to exclude education from the scope of budget cuts, which I support. It is not appropriate to impose undue restrictions during this initial phase of development. I plan to prepare a separate budget that lists the expenses for the educational plan that has already been approved in principle, the expenses for 1932 if it proceeds as planned, and the expenses for the following years to facilitate comprehensive planning. Based on current estimates, 1.5 million taels will be used for education in 1932, which is approximately equal to the revenue from the 2% increase in police rates. Regarding the issue of balancing the 1932 budget, the accounting director stated that even if each department makes cuts to the greatest extent possible, it would be difficult to balance revenue and expenditure if the police rates remain at 1.4%. The council should have requested taxpayers to increase taxes at the last annual meeting of taxpayers, but due to the aforementioned substantial funds carried over from 1930, a tax increase was not proposed. Fluctuations in the exchange rate of the council's pound payments are an important factor in balancing the budget. If the exchange rate for 1932 can reach two shillings, it would save approximately 1.1 million taels compared to the 1931 budget. However, the exchange rate for the next twelve months is difficult to predict, so it is necessary to be somewhat cautious in estimating the exchange rate for certain items. However, even if the council can manage to obtain a favorable exchange rate, it will be difficult to balance the budget without increasing police rates under the current circumstances. The accounting director also stated that in 1927, police rates were increased to 16% due to a budget shortfall, but current expenditures in various departments have increased compared to before. For example, the expenditure index for the Police Department is 113% compared to 1927, and for the Shanghai Volunteer Corps, it is 173%. However, due to the expected increase in exchange rates and the increase in tax revenue from re-evaluating land prices, it is hoped that an increase in police rates to 16% may balance revenue and expenditure, and that the tax rate of 16% is still very low compared to other Western cities. Furthermore, since the Finance Committee meeting in September of last year, the council has ordered the heads of each department to make every effort to cut expenditures during the remaining months of this year, especially when preparing the 1932 budget. The heads of each department have been able to make cuts to the greatest extent possible within their authority, which is deeply satisfying. After discussing the accounting director's proposal, the Finance Committee agreed to the tax increase. However, the financial situation must be reconsidered when determining the 1932 budget. When this proposal was moved to the board meeting for discussion, the accounting director stated that even with the 2% tax increase, the additional revenue of 1.2 million taels is not enough, and further cuts must be made to the expenditures of each department and certain items between the regular and special budgets must be reorganized in order to make up for the shortfall. A director then suggested that the taxpayers' ability to pay should also be considered. The directors then turned to discuss the financial situation of various industries. The accounting director stated that it would not be possible to reduce the budget deficit by as much as 2 million taels while maintaining essential government functions. A director then stated that with Shanghai's prosperity, a police rate of 16% is not inappropriate. Therefore, he advocated that the budget should be prepared based on a 16% tax rate, while providing the citizens with a detailed explanation of the reasons for the tax increase. Finally, it was decided to postpone the decision on this proposal to the next meeting. In the meantime, the Chinese directors will be asked to provide detailed opinions.

Brief Biographies of Korean Patriots Lee Bong-chang and Han Zhi-shi

▲Once Associated with Independence Party Leaders in Shanghai

The Guowen News Agency reports that Lee Bong-chang, the Korean patriot who attempted to assassinate the Japanese Emperor on the 8th of this month, is from Gyeongseong (Seoul), Korea. He was born in Yongsan (Seoul) and is 32 years old this year. He is a graduate of Gyeongseong's Wenchang School. His father's name is Zhenqiu. Bong-chang has one older brother and two younger brothers. After graduating, he worked at the Yongsan Railway Bureau for three or four years. Seven years ago, he went to Osaka to work at the gas factory there. Four years ago, he went to Tokyo and worked in a Japanese store. The following year, he returned to Osaka. Two years ago, he came to Shanghai. At the age of 24, he embraced patriotism and nationalism. However, because he was always among the Japanese, some ridiculed him for being assimilated. But in Lee's heart, he harbored a strong desire to restore his country. Lee's inherited property and land were seized by the Japanese through high-pressure tactics, which further added to his grief over the loss of his country and home. After arriving in Shanghai, he associated with Korean Independence Party leaders in the Hongkou area and received their support. Lee is said to be bold and capable, with a large alcohol capacity.

Upper Yangtze River Shipping Disasters Caused by Shallow Water

▲Piton Near Kongling Shoal Sinks

▲Yibin Loses Control at Chenglingji

Several ships on the Yangtze River have recently had accidents due to shallow water. A summary follows:

▲British Ship The Piton, an Upper Yangtze River merchant ship managed by Butterfield & Swire, loaded a large quantity of cotton yarn, 950 pieces, in Shanghai and set sail for Chongqing. While traveling through the Kongling Shoal section of the river, the water level dropped, and the ship mistakenly ran aground on a reef. The bottom of the ship became lodged on the reef. The shipowner attempted to free the ship from the shoal. At that time, the ship was reversed, and the bottom of the ship was split in two by the reef. River water rushed into the cabin, and the ship immediately sank. The cargo in the cabin sank with the ship. Passengers on board struggled to escape. Fortunately, civilian ships were traveling near Taohe. After the shipowner sent out a distress call, many came to help with the rescue. However, it is not yet clear if there were any deaths or injuries. The broken ship has already sunk into the river. According to yesterday's telegram, the ship is likely to sink and there is no hope of towing it. The losses of the cargo and the ship alone amounted to 300,000 to 400,000 yuan. The damage to passengers and crew is not included.

▲American Ship in Distress The Yibin, a Shanghai-Chongqing liner of the American Merchant Yangtze River Company, transported goods from Shanghai to Chongqing last week. When it arrived at a place 15 miles downstream of Chenglingji, named Taolingji on the river, it encountered low water on the Upper Yangtze River, and the ship became stranded on the sandbar. After the ship was in distress, the shipowner sent out a radio distress call and raised a distress flag. When the Shashi, an Yichang liner of the Taikoo Company, passed upstream, it saw that the Yibin was in distress and went to help. First, a small boat was lowered into the river and approached the Yibin to rescue the passengers in batches and transport them to Yichang to land. At the same time, the Yichang branch of the Merchant Yangtze River Company dispatched its Chunhao merchant ship to Taolingji to transfer the cargo on the Yibin. Unexpectedly, after the ship was stranded, it was hit by a strong wind, and the ship leaned to one side, posing a very dangerous situation. After receiving the news, the insurance company here dispatched personnel to investigate. According to a telegram received by the Shanghai office yesterday, there were still 85 pieces of cotton yarn on board that had not been unloaded, and there was a risk of bandits attacking and looting. The U.S. military ship stationed in Hankou has been requested to sail to protect it. The current survey shows that there is still hope of salvaging the ship, but the construction is quite large and will cost at least 30,000 taels of silver. The passengers have safely gone to Yichang, and there were no casualties.

Entertainment Permit Fees in the French Concession

The French Municipal Council has resolved on the following permit fees for open-air dance halls, theaters, Shanghai opera, male and female storytellers, and brothels within the Concession: Monthly permit for dance halls: 75 taels of silver per permit. Open-air dance halls (gardens or rooftops) will be charged double the above fee. In addition, these venues must pre-pay two months' worth of donation. The permit fee for theaters and cinemas will range from 30 to 200 taels of silver per month, levied based on the size of the venue, as follows: Venues with 500 seats or fewer: 30 taels of silver per month. Venues with 501 to 1,000 seats: 50 taels of silver per month. Venues with 1,001 to 1,500 seats: 100 taels of silver per month. Venues with 1,501 to 2,000 seats: 150 taels of silver per month. Venues with over 2,000 seats: 200 taels of silver per month. The permit fee for Shanghai opera and male/female storytellers will range from 5 to 20 taels per month, based on the size of the venue, and classified as follows: First class: 20 taels per month. Second class: 15 taels per month. Third class: 10 taels per month. Fourth class: 5 taels per month. The permit fee for brothels: 15 yuan per quarter. The permit fee for principal courtesans: 15 yuan per person per quarter. The permit fee for Chinese associations will be divided into three classes: First class: 200 taels per quarter. Second class: 75 taels per quarter. Third class: 25 taels per quarter. The permit fee for film production companies will range from 50 to 25 taels per quarter, divided into three classes: First class: 25 taels. Second class: 15 taels. Third class: 5 taels.
